¶ Sonday. I Am sonday honorable The heed of all the weke dayes That day all thyng labourable. Ought to rest. and gyue lawde & prayes To our creatour. that alwayes Wolde haue vs rest after trauayle Man. seruaunt. and thy beest he sayes And the other to thyn auayle. ¶Monday ¶ Monday. men ought me for to call In whiche. god werkes ought to begyn Heryng masse. te fyrst dede of all Intendyng to fle deedly syn This worldly goodes truly to wyn with labour and true excercyse For who of good werkes can not blyn To rewarde. shall wyn paradyse. ¶Tuesday. ¶ I tuesday. am so named of mars Called of goddes army potent. I loue neuer for to be scars Of werke. but alway dilygent Stryuyng agaynst lyfe indigent Beyng in this worlde: and els where To serue our lorde. with good intent As of duety. we are bounde here.
¶wednesday▪ ¶wednesday. sothely is my name Amyd the weke is my beyng wherin all vertues dooth frame By the meanes of good lyuyng I do remembre the heuen kyng That was solde in my season. I do werke with true meanyng Hym to serue. as it is reason. ¶ Thursday. ¶ I am the meryest of seuen Called thursday veryly. In my tyme the kyng of heuen Made his sowper meryly In fourme of breed gaue his body To his appostles. as is playne And than wasshed theyr fete mekely And went to olyuet mountayne. ¶Fryd ¶ Named I am deuout fryday The whiche careth for no delyte But to mourne. fast. deale. and pray I do set all my hole appetyte To thynke on the Iewes despyte How they dyde Cryst on the tre rend And thynkyng how I may be quyte At the dredefull iugement.
¶ Saterday. ¶ Saterday I am comyng last Trustyng on the tyme spent well Hauyng euer mynde stedfast On that lorde that harowed hell That he my synnes wyl expell At the instaunce of his mother whose goodnesse dooth ferre excell whome I serue aboue all other. ¶  ryn▪ stated out of chi  glysslye by beri Copland prnter at London. FOr to begyn the maner of saluta¦ry of helthfull lyuyng: & to come to perfectyon (how well I haue more nede to be instruct than for to teche other) yet kepe these small doctry¦nes here folowyng to your powers. Fyrst ryse vp at .vj. of the clocke ī the mornyng in all seasons. And in your rysyng do as fo¦loweth. Thanke our lorde of the rest that he gaue you that nyght. Cōmende you to god. to our blyssed lady saynt mary. and

¶  sancti euange  Gloria tibi domine. IN principio erat verbū et verbū erat apud deum et de{us} erat verbū. Hoc erat in principio apud deū. Oīa per ipsum facta sunt: et sine ipso factū est nichil. Qd factū est in ipso vita erat: et vita erat lux hominum. Et lux in tene¦bris lucet / & tenebre eam non comprehen∣derunt. Fuit homo missus a deo: cui nomē erat iohannes. Hic venit in testimonium: vt testimonium perhiberet de lumine / vt omnes crederent per illum. Non erat ille lux: sed vt testimonium perhiberet de lu∣mine. Erat lux vera: que illuminat omnē hominem venientem in hunc mundum. In mundo erat & mūdus per ipsum factus est: et mundus eum non cognouit. In pro∣pria venit: & sui eū non receperunt. Quot quot autem receperunt eum: dedit eis po∣testatem filios dei fieri / his qui credunt in nomine eius. Quinō ex sanguinibus / ne∣{que} ex voluntate carnis / ne{que} ex voluntate viri: sed ex deo nati sunt. Et verbum caro factum est: et habitauit in nobis. Et vidi∣mus

Re∣cumbentibus vnde∣cim discipulis apparuit il¦lis iesus: & exprobrauit in∣credulitatem illo{rum} et du∣riciā cordis: quia his qui viderant eum resurrexis∣se / non crediderant. Et di¦xit eis. Signa au∣tem eos qui crediderint: hec sequentur. In nomine meo demonia eijcient linguis loquentur nouis: serpentes tollent. Et si mortiferum quid biberint: nō eis nocebit. INITIVM SALVTIS NOTITIA PECCATI ¶For this cruell synne Nathan the pro∣phete Dauid reproued: and blamed gretely. wherfore Dauyd with heuynesse replete. Tenderly wepyng cryed: Peccaui.
DOmine ne in furore tuo arguas me: ne{que} in ira tua corripias me. uomam sagitte tue inxe sunt michi: et confirmasti super me manum tuam. ō est sanitas ī carne mea a facie ire tue: nō est pax ossibus meis a facie peccatorum meorum. uoniā iniquitates mee supergresse sunt caput meum: et sicut onus graue grauate sunt super me. utruerunt et corrupte sunt cicatrices mee: a facie infipientie mee. iser factus sum et curuatus sum vs{que} in finem: tota die contristatus ingrediebar. uoniam lumbi mei impleti sunt illusio¦nibus: et non est sanitas in carne mea. Afflictus sum et humiliatus sum nimis: rugiebam a gemitu cordis mei. Dn̄e ante te omne desiderium meum: & ge¦mitus meus a te non est absconditus. or meum cōturbatum est dereliquit me virtus mea: et lumen oculorum meorum & ipsum non est mecum. Amici mei et proximi mei: aduersum me appropinquauerunt et steterunt. Et qui iuxta me erant de longe steterūt: & vim faciebant quiquerebant animā meā.
Et qui inquirebāt mala michi locuti sunt vanitates: & dolos tota die meditantur. A go autem tan{quam} surdus nō audiebam: et sicut mutus non aperiens os suum. Et factus sum sicut homo non audiens: et non habens in ore suo redargutiones. Quoniam in te domine speraui: tu exau∣dies me domine deus meus. Quia dixi nequando supergaudeant mi∣chi inimici mei: et dum commouentur pe∣des mei super me magna locuti sunt. Quoniam ego in flagella paratus sum: et dolor meus in conspectu meo semper. Quoniam iniquitatem meam annuncia∣bo: et cogitabo pro peccato meo. nimici autem mei viuunt et confirmati sunt super me: & multiplicati sunt qui ode∣runt me inique. Qui retribuunt mala pro bonis detrahe∣bant michi: qnoniā sequebar bonitatem. e derelinquas me domine deus meus: ne discesseris a me. Intēde in adiutorium meum: domine de{us} salutis mee. Gloria patri et filio: et spiritui sancto. Sicut erat in principio et nunc et semper et in secula seculorum amen.

MIserere mei deus: secundum magnā misericordiam tuam. Et secūdū multitudinem miserationum tuarum: dele iniquitatem meam. Amplius laua me ab iniquitate mea: et a peccato meo munda me. VERTI AD DN̄M CERTIS SIMA VITA EST Dauyd for his synne gretely dyde com∣playne. Feryng the hate of god for his vyce. Vpon dareuna an hye mountayne. By counsell of God he dyde sacrifice.
DOmine exaudi orationem meam: et clamor meus ad te veniat. on auertas faciem tuam a me: in quacū{que} die tribulor inclina ad me aurē tuam. n quacun{que} die inuocauero te: velociter exaudi me. uia defecerunt sicut fumus dies mei: et ossa mea sicut cremium aruerunt. ercussus sum vt fenum & aruit cor meū: quia oblitus sum comedere panem meum. voce gemit{us} mei: adhesit os meū carni mee. O ies mei sicut vmbra declina¦uerunt: et ego sicut fenum arui. u autem dn̄e in eternū permanes: & me∣morrale tuū in generatiōe & generationē. u exurgens dn̄e misereberis sion: quia tempus miserendi eius quia venit tēpus. uoniam placuerunt seruis tuis lapides
eius: et terre eius miserebuntur. Et timebūt gētes nomē tuum domine: et omnes reges terre gloriam tuam. Qr edificauit dn̄s siō: & videbit{us} ī glia sua. Quia prospexit de excelso sancto suo: do∣minus de celo in terram aspexit. Vt audiret gemitus compeditorū: vt sol∣ueret filios interemptorum. Vt annūciēt in sion nomē dn̄i: et laudem eius in hierusalē. In cōueniēdo populos in vnum: & reges vt seruiant domino. Respondit ei in via virtutis sue: paucita∣tem dierum meorum nuncia michi. Qe reuoces me in dimidio dierū meo{rum}: in generatione et generationem anni tui. Initio tu domine terram fundasti: et ope¦ra manuum tuarum sunt celi. Ipsi peribunt tu autem permanes: & om∣nes sicut vestimentum veterascent. t sicut opertorium mutabis eos & muta¦buntur: tu autem idem ipse es / et anni tui¦nō deficient. ¶ Here foloweth certaynes q̄stiōs what is synne with the ordre of confession. Hyrst. what is penitence? Penitence is the emendacyon of the lyfe with in warde contricyon of hert for the synne committed: with a full purpose neuer do the synne agayn. ¶ Vvhat is the effect of penitence? Penitence maketh aungelles gladde: iustyfyeth wycked persones: cal∣leth agayn the goodnes lost: and draweth mankynde vnto euerlastynge lyfe. ¶ How many necessary thynges be lon∣ge to penitence? Fyue which ben they. Hope of forgyuenes: contricyon of her∣te: confession of the faute: fulfyllyng of suche thynges as the preest shall comma∣unde and enioyne. and vtterly to forsake synne. ¶ How is synne auoyded? By auoydynge occasyon therof: as is pleasu∣sure: the beholdynge of the wanton play∣es: euyll company: and suche other. ¶ Vvho shall neuer be forgyuen? He that forgyueth not to other and he that to his power wyll not restore agayne thyn∣ges wrongfully taken. ¶ How prouest thou that? For it is sayd in the Pater nr̄. Dimitte nobis debita nostra: sicut et nos
dimittim{us} debirorib{us} nr̄is. Good lorde for gyue vs as we forgyue. And saynt Augu∣stin sayth. Nō dimittit{ur} pctm̄ nisi restituat{ur} ablatū. The synne is neuer forgyuen tyll the thynge wrong fully taken be restored. Therfore whā we offende in worde / or in¦dede we oughte to our power make satis∣faccyon. And what euyll wyll / malyce / or hatred we haue cōceyued agaynst ony we sholde put it out of our mynde / to thende that our confessyon may be acceptable to god. ¶ What is cōfessyon? Confessyon is the declaracyon of synne before a prest / or ony other in necessite. ¶ Vnder what ma¦ner ought the confessyon be? True of thy propre synnes hole / spedefull of the sure manerly / voluntarely clere with suche de¦lyberacyon that it may playnly be vnder¦stande: and wit so grete contricyon that it may make the sory & heuy to haue cōmyt∣ted those synnes / fully myndynge neuer to retourne to theym agayne: & so for the surely purposynge to do penaunce. ¶ What sholde I do willyng to be confes∣sed? Before all thynges ī thy bedde / cham¦bre? or other secrete place moche and often tymes thynke by thy selfe / where / how
whan with whome / how many tymes / & how enormely thou hast synned / wether ī spekynge / {con}sēte / wyll / or dede / what good dede thou haste lefte whiche thou ough∣test to haue done. Nor it is not sufficyent to confesse the a lyer: but thou muste hole expresse what yll hath folowed vpon that lye. Nor thou shalt not onely say. I haue synned in glotony but thou must tell how moche whether thou were dronken / or dy¦dest vomyte. c. in what place it was / and how oft. And whan thou diligētly by thy selphe hast discussed and {con}sydered all thyn¦ges / than go thou to the preest with grete reuerence / and not as thou woldest tell a a tale: and after the sygne of the crosse ma¦de vpon thy brest say. Benedicite. Than af¦ter a fewe wordes spoken of the preest / thou shalt {pro}cede in this maner. Confiteor deo celi. &c. tyll thou come to mea culpa. Than begynne to declare how thou hast synned. FYrst I knowlege my selfe gylty vnto almyghty god vnto our lady saynt Mary: and to all the company of heuen and to you my goostly fader: that syth  the tyme of my laste confessyon I haue of¦fended my lorde god greuously / & specyal¦ly in the seuen deedly synnes. ¶ Pryde. I Haue synned in pryde of herte / not lowly thankynge god of gyftes & con¦nynge whiche he hath sent me. Also I ha∣ue synned ī pryde of clothynge: in strēgth: in eloquēce: in beaute: in proude wordes. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶ En ¶Also I haue synned in enuy herynge o∣ny man more praysed thā I or better che∣rysshed with his souerayne than I / or he hath more {pro}sperite than I & whā I haue my sauswered myn euen crysten reioysyn¦ge. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶
¶Also I haue synned in wrathe: as in ry∣gour of herte agaynst myn euen crysten whether it were lytell mater or greate & for euery worde I wylled to be auenged on them and answered them with euyll wordes: and of smytyng them. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶Sloute. ¶ Also I haue synned in slouthe: and spe∣cyally in geuynes of hert: and delyted me in ylde thoughtes and ymaginacyons of the worlde and my flesshe / not thankynge god of his benefyte neyther beynge sory for my synnes nor occupyed myselfe in good prayers nor holy meditacyons for the conforte of my soule. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶Couetyse. ¶Also I haue synned in couetyse by vnle¦full desyres of worldly goodes in misspen∣dynge and vnreasonably kepynge of the∣ym: and I haue / ouermoche desyred welt and prosperite and more worldly worshyp and rychesse than I had / and grutched at tribulacyons / aduersyte and pouerte whe¦rof I cry god mercy. ¶Glotony. ¶Also I haue synned in glotony by vn∣reasonable lustes of metes and drynkes / more for flesshely luste thā for bodyly suste¦naunce
/ and I haue that grete excesse of metes and drynkes so that nature myght not ber it wherby I was the worse dispo∣sed to serue my lorde god and the more sty∣red to synne / wrath / and wrethchednes. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶Lechery. ¶Also I haue synned in lechery / by fou∣le touchyng by thought of fylthy lustes and vnclennes / somtyme in dede done / in pollucyons and felynge of myn owne fles¦she / also in syght of virgyns and wydowes wherof I cry god mercy. ¶ The .x. commaundmentes. ¶Also I haue synned in brekyng of the x. commaundementes. I haue not loued my lorde god aboue all thynge / nor my neyghbours al my selfe. I haue customa¦bly sworne by my lorde god / by his na∣me in vayne / by his swete body and his sayntes all. I haue not halowed the fe∣estes and holy dayes commannded by the chyrche. I haue not done dewe reueren∣ce to my fader and moder nor to my goost∣ly fades / nor folowed theyr techynge. I haue synned in backbitynge myn euen cryste in depravynge of theyr good name
and defylynge them with my wordes. I haue harmed my neyghbours takynge the yr goodes agaynst theyr wyll by wronge. the seke I haue not departed of my goodes to the poore I haue not harboured the har¦borlesse. I ha∣ue not gyuen counseyll to them that had nede. I haue not taught the ignoraunt. I haue not discretly corrected them that have offended. I haue not conforted them that haue ben in heuynes. I haue not deuout¦ly prayed to god for my neyghbour to gy∣ue hym grace to amende his synful lyuyn¦ge and continue in vertue. ¶ The .vij. gyftes of the holy goost. ¶Also I haue not vsed the gyftes of the holy goost to the honour of god: as the gyfte of vnderstandynge: the gyfte of wys¦dome: the gyfte of counseyll: the gyfte: of science: the gyfte of strength: the gyfte of pyte: and the gyfte of drede. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶ The .vij. sacramentes.
¶ Also I haue not gyuen tankes to our lorde forte .vij. sacramentes. As the sa∣crament of baptym: of confirmation: of pe¦naunce: of the body: of our lorde: of wed¦locke: of preest hode: and of enelynge. wherof beynge repentaunt. I cry god mercy. ¶The .viij. beatitudes ¶Also I haue not disposed me to the .viij. beatitudes: as pouerte of spiryte / perfyte mekenes in aduersite / perfyte mekenes in prosperyte / lust of ryght wylnesse / per∣fyte mercy / clennesse of hert: peas in desy∣re. Ioyful suffrance of persecucyon in the cause of vertue. wherof I cry god mercy. ¶ Of these and all other: knowen and not knowen that euer I dyde syth I was borne vnto this daye I aske god mercy: and moost mercy full lorde god. I yelde me gylty vnto the ād vtterly put me vnto thy grace: pyte and mercy: and I praye you my goostly fader to be betwene my synne and me that god of his mercy forgy¦ue me for this lowly cōfessyon that I may be free fro my goostly ennemy ād optayn the endles blysse that god hath bought me to. ¶Ideo deprecor. .
